### Post by IWantFroyo on 2011-09-30
1. Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
2. If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded  picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page  number/page link/etc.
3. Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
4. The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or  suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids  and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to  browse for everyone.
5. The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your  posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
6. Please use reduced-size thumbnails, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
7. To avoid having users having to ask you for them. when possible we  request that you format your posts in the following order: NOTE this is  optional

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed!  Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is  removed, this is why.

ImageShack causes problems for users in some countries. Please use another image hosting service.

Note: Obsteperous means noisy and unruly.

I'm currently installing the Oneiric beta 2 on my Toshiba. I'll probably post back soon with whatever I will have managed to make.

### Post by TeoBigusGeekus on 2011-09-30
It's just Arch linux with openbox stand alone:
Openbox theme: [Turquoise nights ob]("http://box-look.org/content/show.php/?content=120386")
GTK-Theme: [Elegant GTK]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=127826")
Icon Theme: [Areao43]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/area.o43+SVG+Icon+theme?content=101979")
Conky: [My only contribution to open source.]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1156383")

There's no dock, no panel, no nothing.
Openbox uses 1% of cpu power of a P4@3Gh and 90mb of ram at startup.

---

### Post by Whistling Nixie on 2011-09-30
Wallpaper: [*Mint Funky Black*](http://zwopper.deviantart.com/art/Mint-Funky-Black-259452520) by [Zwopper](http://zwopper.deviantart.com/)
Theme: [Mint-X-Metal](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/?content=134015)
Icons: [Mint-X-Faenza](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/?content=135238) (Some icons have been replaced with improved versions)
Nautilus background colour: "Charcoal"
Menu opacity set at 90 (MintMenu > Control Center > CompizConfig Settings Manager > Opacity, Brightness and Saturation)
Font: Ubuntu Font Family

**Terminal**
Text: #b2b2b2
Background: #212121
Username: #accd8a
Font: [Ubuntu Mono](http://www.omgubuntu.co.uk/2011/09/ubuntu-monospace-font-released/)

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2011-10-01
Couple more , of the Alt+Tab feature..

This is Alt+Tab.
Holding alt and pressing tab moves through each open app.
[ATTACH]203285[/ATTACH]

And pressing down arrow while in alt+tab, Shows a preview of that app/window..
like. [ATTACH]203286[/ATTACH]

this is just the "show all windows"  aka my bottom right corner. lol

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2011-10-01
> **Ringi said:**
> Its Ambiance Dark with edit colors

How do I turn of the backlight?

  thanks. 

Do you have CCSM installed?

If so..
Just open it, Go to the "Unity" plugin..
and "Experimental" tab, then change 'backlight mode'
[ATTACH]203294[/ATTACH]
I used to have it set to "off"..
But now it has a new setting. "edge illumination toggles".
which i like alot. :)
nice glow just around the edges.

If you dont have CCSM installed, or dont want to install it..
you can also use gconf-editor, or dconf-editor. 

ohh wait...
Here you go! :lolflag:
this tells all the ways..
[http://askubuntu.com/questions/29553/how-can-i-configure-unity](http://askubuntu.com/questions/29553/how-can-i-configure-unity)
forgot about that.  :)

How do you edit colors?
i cant figure that out in the new GTK3/Unity/ubuntu.. ???

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-02
Integrated Intel can be just fine - it varies chipset to chipset. I've had good luck myself, but that's not guaranteed, particularly on older models that just won't have this or that feature that Unity requires to run. 

I got a couple of new walls that I love to death, and Synapse's new Places feature, sorely missed until now, has made it absolutely the transparent, forgettable center of my Ubuntu experience. I'm still not using Unity, although my reasons are astonishingly petty details that are becoming less relevant even to me the more I look at them.

Poke to make big.

[[img]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/111002/copy%20of%20places.png[/img]](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/111002/places.png)

Y'know, I used to find myself using Alt+F2 to run things because menus were clumsy, but it felt nerdy at the time. Now it's normal. I like that. Synapse just keeps getting better, and it's converted me into a full Zeitgeist fanboi.

I actually got this update with the Places category late, because I'd put off updates for a bit, idly seeing if I could get a month uptime. I had an X crash at 28 days, which of course didn't reset my uptime but made it seem like cheating; after I went ahead and ran the updates, this was a nice consolation.

[[img]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/111002/copy%20of%20walls.png[/img]](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/111002/walls.png)

This is the collection of the four most comforting images I've ever encountered that I could find at at least 10x6.

I've also been making much better use of workspaces of late - I'll have one filled with files I need in class, one with Chrome tabs and windows I'm saving for later, one with an image editing project, etc. and not feel the urge to close anything I'll have to reopen a few hours later. This is one of my petty qualms with Unity: no way to keep windows on other workspaces out of the dock, which makes all this compartmentalization completely worthless. 

However, I also had a dream last night that Compiz had finally implemented KDE-style window spreads in the Expo view, which probably means that this obsession has tipped into an unhealthy range.

[[img]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/111002/copy%20of%20reader.png[/img]](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/111002/reader.png)

I'm experimenting with paying real money for limited access to fake books now that Chrome has a Kindle app with local caching that can pretend to be a native app. Drawbacks include that the interface can't be scaled below 800px wide - so no two-up with a gedit - and paying real money for limited access to fake books.

I've also given up on the Trailfocus / Dim Inactive plugin, which I love, because it seems to have actually become *less* predictable with time in 11.04, and something that is meant to allow me to assess at a glance which window is active and focus on it has instead become a tool for assessing whether or not the plugin is working and focusing on my frustration with the fate of less popular plugins and features.

---

People with eight year old Intel cards usually complain because they can't run the Kwin Blur, lol, at least their laptops are not burning.

And yeah, I haven't used Alt+F2 since switching to Synapse. Seems redundant, even if Alt+F2 (which for me was xfrun4) has better completion for arbitrary commands. If I really need tab completion, I probably need a terminal window, anyway.

### Post by ninjaaron on 2011-10-02

Woah there!  You're using too-spaced-out version that went up for a little while.  I somehow accidentlily grew the spacing by one pixel while I was still figuring out the program.  It's fixed now.  Course, if you like it that way, then more power to ya', but the "offical version" is a little different.
[http://github.com/ninjaaron/bitocra](http://github.com/ninjaaron/bitocra)

I have a feeling the reason it's switching fonts in some places (those smaller letters definitly aren't mine) has to do with the way you call it in .Xresources.  I used to get some font substitutions in weird places when I called it as an X core font, but call it with xft in .Xresources, and I don't get that stuff anymore, since xft is able to generate alternative font styles (bold and italic) based on a regular face...  Or do you have it set up like that on purpose?  I never had anything quite like what's going on on your screen there, even when I mess around in Debian (Speaknig of that, didn't know #! was based on stable.  I though it was based on Testing for some reason.  I switched my Debian partition to Sid for the lulz.  It turns out that it's way less buggy than the 11.10 beta and Fedora 15).

### Post by ilovelinux33467 on 2011-10-03
> **ninjaaron said:**
> 
BTW, is that bash?  Nice multi-colored shell going on there.  I was going to figure out how to do that one of these days, but I haven't gotten around to it yet.


If you want a multicoloured prompt you should try out zsh which has some inbuilt prompt themes. You just have to load the promptinit module like so:
```

autoload -Uz promptinit && promptinit

```
Then to get a list of the available prompt themes run
```

prompt -l

```
and to preview them run
```

prompt -p

```
An example of the clint theme:
[http://ompldr.org/vYW10cg/snapshot12.png]("http://ompldr.org/vYW10cg/snapshot12.png")

---

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2011-10-03
> **Pazit said:**
> Thank you ~el koraco , can you please suggest the one you think I should choose?
I am not happy with the fonts and playing around it didn't help much:(

I even tried to install some but somehow it didn't work out. like I said, still a lot to learn...


I like the Ubuntu font myself. lol ;)
The droid fonts are also nice though.

To install new fonts (.ttf)

First go to your home folder, right click on an empty space, and "create new folder"
name this folder **.fonts** . the period in front of 'fonts' mean it will be a hidden folder. 

 Then, to install new fonts...

You can either..
1.) Double click a font (.ttf) file, and click "Install" when the window pops up.
or
2.) Just drag the font files into your .fonts folder.

You can show hidden files/folders by pressing Ctrl H while in your home (or any other) folder. 

Hope it helps.

---

### Post by ninjaaron on 2011-10-03
> **vehemoth said:**
> Not finished yet
These are three of my current groups (workspaces/virtual desktops)
@ninjaaron love your font, especially the quirky characters such as the square brackets and 8.
Nice.  I like the quirky characters too (I guess I should), and I actually find that they make it easier to recognize characters.  That's the problem with a lot of the fonts that have a novel design approach. Sometimes it hard to figure out which letter your looking at.  That's also why my "S" is a little fugly (at least in my opinion).  Whenever I tried anything else, I had trouble distinguishing it from the number "5."

But if you like the quirks, you should check out some of the ttf-ocr-a fonts as well.  The one in the Ubuntu repos is nice.  Unfortunately, I think they are not hinted, so they get blurry at smaller sizes.  That's the main reason my font exists.

@el_koraco.  Vimtutor is nice, but the real way to learn after you do it is to put vim everywhere else, especially in your browser (pentadactyl FTW!).  Once you learn the bindings, you find that they work in almost all of your terminal apps (mostly pagers and curses type stuff, of course, though you can also get shells with vi bindings; i.e. zsh).

### Post by ninjaaron on 2011-10-04
A journalist took some quality pictures of my tattoos for a story he wants to write, so they are in this screenshot.  

Distro: Arch
WM: scrotwm
Wallpaper from the Oneiric proposed pack.
Music player: ncmpcpp
Image viewer: gqview

[[IMG]http://ubuntuone.com/0DAeZ4fjbtlXFMEQnuojxO[/IMG]]("http://ubuntuone.com/6YWoud46HegRxdEOrBqxGi")

Background:
Tat under my clavicle is Greek, in a script I made from an SVG trace of [Codex Sinaticus]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Codex_Sinaiticus"), the oldest complete manuscript of the New Testament (circa 350 CE).

Transliteration:
hina agapat&#275; all&#275;lous

Translation:
That you may love one another
(as in "these things I command you in order that you may love one another").

Tat on my sholder in a Paleo-Hebrew script, imitated from the letters as they appear in the [Siloam Inscription]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siloam_inscription"), which dates to ~700 BCE.

Transliteration:
yhwh shoftenu
yhwh m'choqeqenu
yhwh malkenu
hu yoshi'enu

This one contains a bit more pointed of religious message than ought to be posted on forum as devoutly agnostic as UF.  The curious can look it up in Isaiah 33:22.

Those with comments or questions about the actual text of either tattoo are welcome to PM me or email me (ninjaaron@gmail.com), but obviously public discussions are forbidden by the forum CoC.  Comments about the tattoos themselves or the scripts should be ok, I suppose.

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2011-10-04
> **Pazit said:**
> Thank you once more.
I already faved LaGaDesk for it:)
if you just could give me an explanation on how to use conky I will be more than happy to get your conky script.
 Last time that I tried  using conky I ended up like this  ](*,) :(

Sure,
Yeah conky can make you want to bash your head on a wall sometimes, but this one is rather simple to "setup"

Here is the conky , in a zip file.~ [http://ubuntuone.com/p/12WE/](http://ubuntuone.com/p/12WE/)

edit: oh yeah, make sure you have conky installed first lol :P

then...
1.) Unzip the file

2.) Extract the 3 items to, lets say - your desktop.

3.) Install the font~ (double click it and click the "install" button when the window pops up.)  [ or just move it to your .fonts folder]

4.) Move the "conky-103-bg.png" image into your home folder. [this is where it will stay]

5.) move the "conkyrc" file into your home folder also, and right click it, rename, and just put a period in front of the 'conkyrc'. So it would be named .conkyrc

Once those things are done..

Just open a terminal, 
type in the word **conky**,
and press enter.
It should toss up a pretty conky onto the right side of your desktop. 

That should be it.

Let me know how it goes or if you have a problem.

I'm not real great when it comes to conkys..
and can do only simple things with them..
But this is one of the easiest ive ever used. lol ;) 

Good luck, have fun!

---

### Post by Pazit on 2011-10-04
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> Sure,
Yeah conky can make you want to bash your head on a wall sometimes, but this one is rather simple to "setup"

Here is the conky , in a zip file.~ [http://ubuntuone.com/p/12WE/](http://ubuntuone.com/p/12WE/)

edit: oh yeah, make sure you have conky installed first lol :P

then...
1.) Unzip the file

2.) Extract the 3 items to, lets say - your desktop.

3.) Install the font~ (double click it and click the "install" button when the window pops up.)  [ or just move it to your .fonts folder]

4.) Move the "conky-103-bg.png" image into your home folder. [this is where it will stay]

5.) move the "conkyrc" file into your home folder also, and right click it, rename, and just put a period in front of the 'conkyrc'. So it would be named .conkyrc

Once those things are done..

Just open a terminal, 
type in the word **conky**,
and press enter.
It should toss up a pretty conky onto the right side of your desktop. 

That should be it.

Let me know how it goes or if you have a problem.

I'm not real great when it comes to conkys..
and can do only simple things with them..
But this is one of the easiest ive ever used. lol ;) 

Good luck, have fun!

See my terminal :confused:

### Post by ilovelinux33467 on 2011-10-04
> **IWantFroyo said:**
> Does Konsole support transparency?

Yes. Right click -> Configure Current Profile -> Appearance Tab -> Edit... -> Background transparency. You may need to enable desktop effects first before transparency will work.

### Post by miimnon on 2011-10-04
This is my screenshot.
Put this in your .bashrc. 
Use it to replace your PS1 variable.

```
    let n=232

    _cmd(){
        if [ "$n" -lt 255 ] ; then
            let n++
        else
            let n=232
        fi
        PS1="\[\033[38;05;${n}m\][\t] \w \! \$ $? $clr_off " 
    }
    PROMPT_COMMAND=_cmd
```

[[IMG]http://img26.imageshack.us/img26/8795/screenul.jpg[/IMG]]("http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/26/screenul.jpg/")

Wtf is going on with the font rendering? I see audacios doesn't look half so crappy. Did you try replicating your fonts.conf values to .Xdefaults/.Xresources as well? My Libreoffice was looking like this until I added 

```
Xft.antialias: 1
Xft.hinting: true
Xft.hintstyle: hintfull
Xft*dpi: 96
Xft.rgba: rgb
```

Yes, that is Ubuntu. Yes, that is the Mint-X theme from Linux Mint... only I'm using the regular Ubuntu Mono Dark icons (based on Humanity) instead of the Mint X ones. Gotta keep it somewhat Ubuntu :) I also changed the AWN theme to Light to match the rest of the Mint X system theme.

Links to the theme and icons are here:
[http://packages.linuxmint.com/pool/main/m/mint-x-icons/](http://packages.linuxmint.com/pool/main/m/mint-x-icons/)
[http://packages.linuxmint.com/pool/main/m/mint-x-theme/](http://packages.linuxmint.com/pool/main/m/mint-x-theme/)

Download the .deb files, the latest versions. Open them to bring up the Ubuntu software center. Install the mint-x-icons first, then the mint-x-theme.

Overall, I like how it looks. But this was just me playing with a Linux Mint theme on my netbook. So it's not a permanent change. I'm back to my regular Ambiance theme.

I know that's how it's supposed to go..
Im just unsure still... :P
Here's what I do...

Pre-alpha 1 is the best time to do a fresh install (final release) IMO.

[LIST]
[*]Wipe the root partition (but **[COLOR="Red"]NOT[/COLOR]** /home).
[*]Do a fresh install of the Final Release.
[*]Put Humpty Dumpty back together again.
[*]Upgrade to Pre-alpha 1 when it hits the repos.
[*]Enjoy 2-3 weeks of bliss.
[*]Then, "let the breakage begin"... :)
[/LIST]


> **Rasa1111 said:**

### Post by VinDSL on 2011-10-07
> **Rasa1111 said:**
>  in regards to the /home partition..
That is something I still have not done yet.
Mostly because I am not totally sure how. 

Im going to need explicit, (instructions for dummies) when that time comes.
Everything Ive read on it, is more confusing to me than Im fully comfortable with. 

 Ive been wanting to do that the past few installs.. 
But have not yet.
I use GParted to setup my drive(s).  It's sort of like a text editor for partitions.  LoL!

Here's an example (the dual-booter I'm on now):


[INDENT](Click to expand)

[[IMG]http://vindsl.com/images/vindsl-desktop-6-oct-2011-3(650x520).png[/IMG]]("http://vindsl.com/images/vindsl-desktop-6-oct-2011-3.png")[/INDENT]



[LIST]
[*]150 GB HDD - divided in half
[*]2 x 10 GB Root partitions
[*]2 x 63 GB /Home partitions
[*]2 x 1 GB  /Swap partitions
[/LIST]

The trick, if you will, is telling the Ubu installer NOT to format /home (during the fresh install).

When you get ready to do it, just start a new thread, and I'm sure many, many, ppl will help you out - call it pay back time.  :)

### Post by ninjaaron on 2011-10-07
> **koleoptero said:**
> That's what the title of your song is saying, and it means dead Christ (sorry to all the Christians out there, I don't mean to offend, just stating what it says).

And the name of the Album appears to be &#1489;&#1506;&#1500; &#1506;&#1511;&#1512;&#1493;&#1503;, Ba'al being the common appelation of the Caananite god of Storms and fertility, Hadad, and eventually king of the pantheon as steward of El.  Ekron is the name of a town in Israel/Palestine, where the god Ba'al apparently had a temple (one of many places).  There's a story where this god is mentioned in the Bible.  It's the one that's also called Baal Zebub, "Lord of the Fly," which is probably a word-play on what was originally Ba'al Zabul, which is actually attested in Caananite documents, and means 'Mightly Lord.'

Sorry.  I get excited when I see things related to my studies.

### Post by Drone4four on 2011-10-08

---

### Post by VinDSL on 2011-10-08
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> Vin, 
Can you tell me how to replace that frumpy "frosty the snowman"/'head & shoulders"  like icon? 
That thing bugs me also. lol  :P
No problem...
[LIST]
[*]Navigate to ~/.icons/ACYL_Icon_Theme_0.9.4/scalable/**[COLOR="Red"]real_icons/apps[/COLOR]**


[*]Right-click on the "**[COLOR="Blue"]preferences-user-information.svg[/COLOR]**" icon


[*]Select "Make Link"


[*]Right-click the symlink that was created


[*]Select "Rename" and change the symlink name to "**[COLOR="Blue"]avatar-default.svg[/COLOR]**"


[*]Move the symlink to ~/.icons/ACYL_Icon_Theme_0.9.4/**[COLOR="Red"]scalable/status[/COLOR]**


[*]Log-out & Log-in (to Unity)
[/LIST]

That's it...  ;)

---

Wallpaper: [*Wallpaper for Mint 39*](http://malvescardoso.deviantart.com/art/Wallpaper-for-Mint-39-202921812?q=gallery:malvescardoso/29189656&qo=51) by [malvescardoso](http://malvescardoso.deviantart.com/)

Icons: [Mint-X-Faenza](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/?content=135238) (Some icons have been replaced with improved versions)

Font: Ubuntu Font Family

**Terminal**
Text: #accd8a
Background: #212121

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2011-10-09
> **VinDSL said:**
> No problem...
[LIST]
[*]Navigate to ~/.icons/ACYL_Icon_Theme_0.9.4/scalable/**[COLOR=Red]real_icons/apps[/COLOR]**
[*]Right-click on the "**[COLOR=Blue]preferences-user-information.svg[/COLOR]**" icon
[*]Select "Make Link"
[*]Right-click the symlink that was created
[*]Select "Rename" and change the symlink name to "**[COLOR=Blue]avatar-default.svg[/COLOR]**"
[*]Move the symlink to ~/.icons/ACYL_Icon_Theme_0.9.4/**[COLOR=Red]scalable/status[/COLOR]**
[*]Log-out & Log-in (to Unity)
[/LIST]

That's it...  ;)

### Post by gutterslob on 2011-10-11
> **el_koraco said:**
> Don't care. If I'm upgrading, I want multiarch and systemd (if I go Sid) and everything. Debian 6.0.3 sucks, I'm getting about 5 degrees more on the card, which is enough to scrap the whole thing.That's the thing with Stable. It works flawlessly and is juggernaut stable for 95% of people, but if you're in that 5% that has issues, the nature of the beast means that non-critical (in their eyes) fixes take a loooong time to come. 

That why I tend to prefer Unstable/Sid when it comes to Debian. You get breakage, but fixes come thick and fast. Not sure if systemd has made its way to Unstable yet, though. It's there in the repos, but I dunno if they've decided to give it priority yet (as in, release an updated apt that automatically pulls it upon a dist-upgrade). I run GRML with the old fashioned file-rc and rebuilt packages, so I'm not quite sure what's happening with regular default Debian Sid at the moment.


On topic: Same old, minimal tweakage

[[IMG]http://ompldr.org/vYXJkbQ.png[/IMG]]("http://ompldr.org/vYXFmMQ")

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2011-10-11
> **Ringi said:**
> 10/10  :p
:mrgreen:
> **not found said:**
> Agreed... awesome wallpaper and 10/10 for the customization to go with it...


404
:mrgreen: x2
> **mips said:**
> Oooo, very nice! Please tell us more about how you got that please?
Well, it's ubuntu 10.10 but that doesn't matter so...

Theme is Equinox Evolution which you can get by
```
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:tiheum/equinox && sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get install equinox-theme
```

Icon theme is AnyColorYouLike set to the same color that the girl on the background is, inherited by that stripped version of faenza I made in august ([link]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/1612038/Faenza-stripped.tar.gz")). Just set the Faenza-stripped to inherit the ACYL icon theme (folder name).

Dock (bottom and top) is avant window navigator, bottom one is for the launchers and the menu (cairo menu) and autohides (window dodge), top one has the indicators, notification area and clock and is always visible. Both of them are set to "none" with a 0px offset and 0 on the reflections alpha.

Ditched the gnome-panel with the barbaric solution
```
sudo chmod -x /usr/bin/gnome-panel
```

And the wallpaper is from simpledesktops.

I also use nautilus elementary and some other apps that don't have a menubar so I had to tweak the theme by
```
gedit /usr/share/themes/Equinox\ Evolution/gtk-2.0/gtkrc
```
and remove the # from the beginning of the two include lines that have them at the bottom of the document (one is for elementary nautilus, the other is for using a globalmenu).

The term colors were nicked from gutterslob at some point, I'll post them if you want them.

Fonts are obvious I assume.

That's about it isn't it?

Oh and since you don't get the run dialog without the gnome panel, I installed gmrun and set it to run with alt+f2 from the commands plugin in compiz.
> **el_koraco said:**
> Don't care. If I'm upgrading, I want multiarch and systemd (if I go Sid) and everything. Debian 6.0.3 sucks, I'm getting about 5 degrees more on the card, which is enough to scrap the whole thing. I'm just too lazy to start. 

Btw, i just put the exact same wallpaper as you on my sister's Natty the other day.
Wonderful wall isn't it? :D

And I agree debian stable is too stable whenever it is. If you also have problems with it then for heaven's sake ditch it.

### Post by el_koraco on 2011-10-11
> **gutterslob said:**
> That's the thing with Stable. It works flawlessly and is juggernaut stable for 95% of people, but if you're in that 5% that has issues, the nature of the beast means that non-critical (in their eyes) fixes take a loooong time to come. 


I managed to wrestle back control of my card by the end of the day. And the second machine i upgraded from Statler to Sid went to the crapper, and is now a staging ground for a battle with an Oneiric mini iso that refuses to boot. The annoying thing about Debian is the hostility towards ATI. I mean, Debian is generally hostile to prop drivers, but the whole attitude towards ATI is awesome, a lot of users have convinced themselves they should run the open source drivers because they're *better*. They're good, but not better, the only thing that's better is actual support. 

Anyhoo, since the dist-upgrade from Squeeze seems like a lost cause (too much customization and uncompatible software), I'm thinking I'll either stick with Squeeze until the next breakage cycle, do a netinstall, put in a 'pure' variety like aptosid or GRML, or go with Ubuntu or Arch. I dd-ed the Arch netinstall iso to my flash drive, will see tomorrow. 

In the meanwhile, zebra-time again! 

[[img]http://ompldr.org/tYXJtdQ[/img]](http://ompldr.org/vYXJtdQ)

### Post by viperdvman on 2011-10-12
Just added something to my Ubuntu on both my desktop and my netbook. Full-screen screenshots here here:

[http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbu5m.jpg](http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbu5m.jpg)
[http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuNet4m.jpg](http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuNet4m.jpg)

Yes, that is the Mint Menu, the very same one that both Linux Mint and Fusion Linux use. I got it from the Webupd8 PPA's. Link here: [http://www.webupd8.org/2011/05/mintmenu-ppa-updated-for-ubuntu-1104.html](http://www.webupd8.org/2011/05/mintmenu-ppa-updated-for-ubuntu-1104.html). I have it running on 11.04 in Ubuntu Classic mode with no problems. I'm sure it'll run on 10.04 and 10.10 as well (I believe the PPA has Mint Menu for those versions as well)

Overall, I like it far better than the regular GNOME Menu (the 3-tabbed one with apps, places, and system). Plus I get the App search function that Unity, GNOME Shell, and KDE's menu have. I would highly recommend it for anyone still running Ubuntu with GNOME 2.x like me.

### Post by slackthumbz on 2011-10-13
Sick of bugs, weird behaviour and general resource hoggery I've given up on gnome-shell and unity for now and switched over to xfce4.8 on Oneiric and I have to say I've fallen in love with my desktop all over again. It's such a breath of fresh air to have a DE that doesn't assume it knows how I work better than I do and actually gives me the flexibility I want. You can't even change the icon set or customise the gtk/window borders in unity/gnome-shell without installing gnome-tweak-tool and having to pull in gnome-shell at the same time (oh great, more bloat) I'm seriously disappointed with the GNOME devs and the Ubuntu team for taking so much of what made linux desktop environments fun away from us.

GTK-2/3 Theme: Greybird 
Icons        : Faenza

> That's one hell of a nice windows theme though I am a bit suprised to see that your icon theme isn't grey.

Changing window's icons is a major pain. Even if you find a complete icon pack, you have to have some kind of app that changes all the icons. And then that usually only works for the default windows icons, and not your apps, so that means you have to manually change all the app icons.

There was a faenza icon pack for windows that installed for all the default icons, which left just the app icons. It looked nice and I don't want to do all of that over again.

### Post by slackthumbz on 2011-10-14
> **ninjaaron said:**
> It is not.

gnome-tweak is not dependent on gnome-shell but gnome-tweak-tool is. It's just that the two projects have such similar names that people are prone to confusion.

And it's gnome-tweak-tool that you need if you want a GUI to configure things like the GTK theme or your icon set or window borders in 11.10...

That was pretty much the straw that broke the camels back for me and made me ditch gnome3 and unity altogether in favour of something that actually did what I wanted and gave me the tools to do it easily.

---

### Post by ninjaaron on 2011-10-14
> **slackthumbz said:**

### Post by Legendary_Bibo on 2011-10-14
What I'm liking about this release is that both my HDMI output and Wacom tablet are working. Although my graphics card isn't performing as well (windows lag when dragged around the screen)

I'm using the Radeon drivers because for some reason the FGLRX drivers are even worse with the window dragging problem and it has a weird glitch with the shadows. Usually the FGLRX drivers are great, and the Radeon one would suck.

---

### Post by kaldor on 2011-10-14
> **Legendary_Bibo said:**
> What I'm liking about this release is that both my HDMI output and Wacom tablet are working. Although my graphics card isn't performing as well (windows lag when dragged around the screen)

I'm using the Radeon drivers because for some reason the FGLRX drivers are even worse with the window dragging problem and it has a weird glitch with the shadows. Usually the FGLRX drivers are great, and the Radeon one would suck.

<offtopic>

The Radeon drivers should be great for stability. It's just the heat issues and lack in performance that are problematic. Should be fine for regular use. If you're not doing any gaming or HD playback, then I'd recommend the OSS drivers. Eventually the free drivers should be decent enough to replace FGLRX for most people. Sorry, I'm a bit of a nut for free drivers :)

---

### Post by Legendary_Bibo on 2011-10-14
> **kaldor said:**
> <offtopic>

The Radeon drivers should be great for stability. It's just the heat issues and lack in performance that are problematic. Should be fine for regular use. If you're not doing any gaming or HD playback, then I'd recommend the OSS drivers. Eventually the free drivers should be decent enough to replace FGLRX for most people. Sorry, I'm a bit of a nut for free drivers :)

The heat problem I used to have the last time I tried the Radeon drivers aren't as bad as it used to be, but sometimes my CPU will suddenly jump to 20% from compiz and 20% from X at random times.

I'm more of a person who uses what works best.

### Post by el_koraco on 2011-10-14
> **Legendary_Bibo said:**
> The heat problem I used to have the last time I tried the Radeon drivers aren't as bad as it used to be, but sometimes my CPU will suddenly jump to 20% from compiz and 20% from X at random times.


If you're gonna be using radeon, you might want to try and update your mesa and X and the driver itself via xorg-edgers or x-swat. Ubuntu's version of X is lagging behind (though fglrx doesn't work with the higher versions). I can't really promise you won't brick your system if you do try it, but if you partitioned right... :D

Just replaced the Kubuntu 11.04 on my Kubuntu LiveUSB with 11.10, and already configured it and set it up how I want to. I like being able to run this on both my netbook and desktop. Granted, I don't get desktop effects, but eh. Here are a pair of screenshots of **_[COLOR="Blue"]Kubuntu 11.10[/COLOR]_** on my netbook:

Full-size images here (1024x600):
[Screenshot 1]("http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotKubuNetN1.jpg")
[Screenshot 2]("http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotKubuNetN1a.jpg")

Note, this is KDE Plasma Netbook. I can easily switch to KDE Plasma Desktop, and already have that mode mostly set up too. The first screenshot is KDE Plasma Netbook in the default Search & Launch workspace. The background is a custom Kubuntu one I downloaded somewhere (Googled it). The second screenshot is KDE Plasma Netbook in a Folder View workspace I added, viewing the folder on my SD card that contains my Legend of Zelda fanfiction. The background is one that I made myself with a forest background and a few pictures from thezeldaproject.net.

Yes, I like playing around with KDE Plasma. However, the KDE Plasma on my Ubuntu 11.04 install isn't as complete of a KDE environment as Kubuntu's. So I do keep a persistent LiveUSB of Kubuntu around. Now it's upgraded to 11.10. I'll have more screenshots of my Kubuntu 11.10 LiveUSB soon. I'll also post Ubuntu 11.10 screenshots when I install it on my desktop alongside 11.04. Oh, and I'll post any updates to my Ubuntu 11.04 from both computers, as usual.

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-15
No, it's Gnome, with Unity turned off and AWN+DBX.

I mean, Orta will work under XFCE, and the decorator is (modified from) the Emerald theme, but I've had bad experiences with the rat. I just like Thunar, primarily in that it loads and renders more quickly, so I have it set as my default file manager. I also have the daemon running, which means it starts even faster, but because of this, it also tries to mount media when I attach them and complains that Nautilus got to it first. Annoying.

If it was really a choice between the two, I'd rather have Nautilus, but Thunar is nice when I don't need a real file manager and just need to grab some stuff.

Compulsive tweaking combined with insomnia, but I made [_one last tweak_]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/10142011/Screenshot.png") to my DockBarX theme. Rather than dimming, groups with minimized windows just get an extra little "something is stuck down here" arrow in the lower corner.

[[img]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/10142011/copyScreenshot.png[/img]]("http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/10142011/Screenshot.png")

### Post by ninjaaron on 2011-10-16
> **urukrama said:**
> Openbox with the Erthe themes, and the AnyColorYouLike icons.

[http://i.imgur.com/FxV1cl.jpg](http://i.imgur.com/FxV1c.jpg)That's a very attractive setup.

herbstluftwm is blowing my effing mind. I think it's love.  The algorithm is somewhere between auto-tiling and manual tiling.  You start with a 'frame,' and the frame will tile vertically, horizontally, as a grid, or with one window taking the frame at a time with windows hidden below.  The trick is that a frame can be split vertically or horizontally and resized as desired.  This makes it a little more futsy than an auto-tiler, but much more versatile. Naturally, it also has a floating mode

But that isn't the genius of herbstluftwm.  The genius is that the manager runs as a server, and is completely controlled by client shell commands.  The configuration file is a shell script, and the window control keybindings execute shell commands.  This means several things:
[list][#] It can be reconfigured and managed from the termnial.
[#] Windows, layouts, and settings can be controlled with scripts
[#] These scripts and commands can be set to keybindings.
[#] You can use any shell command in the config file the way you would in any other script.[/list]

---

### Post by Legendary_Bibo on 2011-10-17
> **ArtF10 said:**
> Could you please post how you installed the icons and theme? Include as many details as possible, for all the steps.

It would really help a lot of us.

For icons you need to create a folder

[I]~/.icons

[/I]For themes

*~/.themes*

Then stick your icons and theme folders in them (you need to extract them).

Then you need to install the Gnome tweak tool, and the icons, and theme will pop up. To change the Shell theme there's some ppa you have to add and then you have to get an extension to the Gnome Tweaker so you can install shell themes.

It's not as simple as Gnome2, but eh it's not that difficult.

---

### Post by koleoptero on 2011-10-17
> **ArtF10 said:**
> Could you please post how you installed the icons and theme? Include as many details as possible, for all the steps.

It would really help a lot of us.

[SIZE="3"]**[COLOR="DarkRed"]The amazing, extraordinary, guide to theme your gnome-shell for dummies.[/COLOR]**[/SIZE]

*[COLOR="DimGray"](assuming you're running gnome-shell already)[/COLOR]*

**1.** Open a terminal and add the following ppas:

```
sudo add-apt-repository ppa:tiheum/equinox ppa:webupd8team/gnome3 ppa:webupd8team/themes
```

**2.** Update the sources:

```
sudo apt-get update
```

**3.** Install necessary things:

```
sudo apt-get install gnome-tweak-tool faenza-icon-theme gnome-shell-extensions-user-theme gnome-shell-extensions-weather zukitwo-theme-all
```

**4.** Press alt+f2 and type "r" without the quotes and hit enter to restart the shell.

**5.** Open the "Advanced Settings" program.

**6.** Go to the "Desktop" tab, and disable the filemanager managing the desktop or you'll get a weird menu behind the shell's top panel when it's transparent.

**7.** Go to "Shell Extensions" tab and turn them on.

**8.** Go to the "Theme" tab and select zukitwo everywhene, and faenza-dark as the icons.

**9.** Restart the shell again.

**10.** To configure the weather indicator see [CLICKY](http://www.webupd8.org/2011/10/install-gnome-shell-weather-extension.html#more)

**11.** Install any other themes you find by extracting them and then copying ***the folder that contains*** the gtk-3.0, gtk-2.0, etc folders into ~/.themes (beware it's hidden :P) Also put any icon themes in ~/.icons (beware, it's hidden too :P)

**12.** ????????

**13.** PROFIT!!!

---

### Post by el_koraco on 2011-10-19
> **krakket said:**
> 
How did you get the panel to look like that?  I like the simple look and the colors...can you customize the blue text to be another color or font?

It's a built in panel of the [scrotwm]("https://opensource.conformal.com/wiki/scrotwm") window manager. You can set the panel font in any color you like. There are lighter panels than Gnome's, tint2 being one of the best, though they lack certain features (or bloat, as some might say). But at least you can go beyond the 21 px limit.

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2011-10-19
If you guys want to try it out..
Here is the code..

 Just copy and paste it into the "code view" tab in your ACYL icon settings window. 
Click "refresh", and then "apply". 
[ATTACH]204877[/ATTACH]

```
<linearGradient
gradientTransform="translate(0,-1004.3622)"
xlink:href="#linearGradient22"
id="linearGradient1234"
x1="24"
y1="1038.2201"
x2="24"
y2="1004.3622"
gradientUnits="userSpaceOnUse" />
<linearGradient
id="linearGradient22">
<stop
style="stop-color:#393834;stop-opacity:1;"
offset="0"
id="stop1" />
<stop
id="stop2"
offset="0.87323946"
style="stop-color:#3c3b37;stop-opacity:1;" />
<stop
style="stop-color:#5d5a51;stop-opacity:1;"
offset="1"
id="stop3" />
</linearGradient>
<linearGradient
id="linearGradient4321">
<stop
style="stop-color:#000000;stop-opacity:1.0;"
offset="0.0"
id="stop1" />
</linearGradient>
<linearGradient
inkscape:collect="always"
xlink:href="#linearGradient4321"
id="acyl_gradient"
x1="50.0%"
y1="0.0%"
x2="50.0%"
y2="100.0%" />
<filter id="filter1111" x="-50%" y="-50%" width="200%" height="200%">
<feImage
id="feImage1"
xlink:href="#1"
result="result1" />
<feComposite
id="feComposite3633"
in2="result1"
in="SourceGraphic"
operator="out" />
</filter>
<defs>
<use id="1" transform="translate(24,24) scale(0.8) translate(-24,-24)" style="" xlink:href="#path-main" />
</defs>
<path
style="fill:#EEEDEB;"
d="m 48,29.547 0,6.5837 C 48,42.7063 42.706288,48 36.130692,48 L 11.869308,48 C 5.293711,48 0,42.7063 0,36.1307 l 0,-6.5837 48,0 z"
id="rect1" />
<path
style="fill:url(#linearGradient1234);"
d="m 11.869308,-1.995842e-7 24.261384,0 C 42.706288,-1.995842e-7 48,5.2936998 48,11.8693 l 0,21.9886 -48,0 0,-21.9886 C 0,5.2936998 5.293711,-1.995842e-7 11.869308,-1.995842e-7 z"
id="rect2" />
<circle transform="translate(24,24) scale(0.7) translate(-24,-21)" cx="24" cy="24" r="24" fill="#EEEDEB"/>
<circle transform="translate(24,24) scale(0.5) translate(-24,-20)" cx="24" cy="24" r="24" fill="#DE4815" style="filter:url(#filter1111)"/>
```
:)

### Post by sanderd17 on 2011-10-19
> **Kexolino said:**
> Seems like Unity and Gnome Shell don't play nice together... GS just froze for me too every time I entered an "a" in the search... But I'm guessing it would play nicer with a mini iso, without Unity.

What theme are you using?

Gnome Shell 3.2 only works with 3.2 themes. You won't notice a difference at first (except a little pixel shift for the top bar), but search just crashes with the old theme (if the seach also contains contacts). So if you're fast enough to tipe 'fir', and there is no contact with a name that begins with 'fir', than search will work. But in cases where the search contains a contact, it will just cause 100% CPU usage.

### Post by koleoptero on 2011-10-19
> **Rasa1111 said:**
> Is there an easy way to do that here? 
Keep everything using the icons, except the top panel?
That would be awesome. :)

[SIZE="3"][COLOR="DarkRed"]The awesome guide to have mono icons in the panel for whatever iconset[/COLOR][/SIZE]

**1.** Go to /usr/share/icons, select and copy the ubuntu-mono-dark and ubuntu-mono-light folders to ~/.icons

**2.** Rename the copied folders to whatever-mono-dark and whatever-mono-light respectively.

**3.** Open a terminal and do
```
cd ~/.icons/whatever-mono-dark
nano index.theme
```
change the line that says Name=... to say the whatever-mono-dark instead of ubuntu
change the line that says Inherits=... to inherit your icon theme instead of Humanity (leave the gnome and hicolor after it if they're there). **Warning:** Use the folder name of the icon theme, not what it shows in appearance settings or gnome-tweak-tool or whatever.
Save the file (ctrl+o) exit nano (ctrl+x) and close the terminal.

**4.**Repeat all the steps in **3** for whatever-mono-light.

**5.**Select the whatever-mono-dark (or light) theme from the tool you use.

**6.**??????

**7.**PROFIT

---

### Post by Larkspur on 2011-10-19

Good stuff! much appreciated. :KS

As well as what Koleoptero advises, you might want to go into the ubuntu-mono-dark folders you copied and check in Places to see if there are home folder icons hanging around.  Make sure you check all the sizes.

Earlier on, you asked what I meant by "small and fidgety": what I meant was that the dash icons are hard to identify at first glance; the detail is too small, at least for my eyes; if you make the detail more prominent, this won't be a problem.

### Post by Larkspur on 2011-10-19

Not sure what to do there. lol  

Since you copied the original ubuntu-mono folders, just go ahead and delete all of them.  The system will use your home folder icons if it can't find them in those Places folders.

### Post by Kexolino on 2011-10-20
> **sanderd17 said:**
> What theme are you using?

Gnome Shell 3.2 only works with 3.2 themes. You won't notice a difference at first (except a little pixel shift for the top bar), but search just crashes with the old theme (if the seach also contains contacts). So if you're fast enough to tipe 'fir', and there is no contact with a name that begins with 'fir', than search will work. But in cases where the search contains a contact, it will just cause 100% CPU usage.

I think you're right, I did use an older Shell theme to match Ambiance, maybe that was the problem then. I didn't have any contacts, so I don't know about that, but this version thing is good to know.

---

### Post by ilovelinux33467 on 2011-10-21
> **Copper Bezel said:**
> No one's posted a KDE screenie in a few pages what with all the Gnome 3 and the XFCE-because-Gnome-3, but I have quick KDE question, and I'm not certain where else to put it. It's something I've wanted to ask with almost every KDE screenshot I've seen.

Is it possible to get rid of the little "bleeding kidney" settings icon on the panel, desktop, etc.?

Install the "I hate the cashew" plasmoid (On Fedora 16 Beta the package is called kde-plasma-ihatethecashew but it should be called something similar in Ubuntu) and add it as a widget to your desktop and it will get rid of the cashew on the desktop :). To get rid on the one on your panel simply lock your widgets (Right click desktop -> Lock Widgets).

---

Seems to make everything go haywire.

### Post by Legendary_Bibo on 2011-10-22
> **koleoptero said:**
> Nice job with theming the panel. Care to share theme details?

The panel background is Vista's taskbar set at 75% opacity (in GIMP, in XFCE's settings it would make the icons partly transparent). You need XFCE's compositing on to make it work though (transparency and all).

Icons are Faenza-Dark, and the theme is Axiom, but I might change that.

Edit:

My taskbar background.

[IMG]http://i.imgur.com/KulKH.png[/IMG]

Gimp it until your heart's content.

### Post by stanca on 2011-10-23
> **vehemoth said:**
> How do you get the background behind the conky? is it just part of your wallpaper or done another way?
I edited the .conkyrc file this way: 
```
own_window_type normal
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_argb_visual yes
own_window_argb_value 0
```It works on E17 too.I haven't tried it on KDE4 yet.
Enjoy it! :):P

---

### Post by Legendary_Bibo on 2011-10-23
> **TheNosh said:**
> ...You're using Gnome Shell AND Xfce4-panel? At that point I find myself wondering why you don't just use Xfce.

Yes, I agree with this. You'll want to remove some gnome packages when transitioning to XFCE though. Some Gnome stuff tends to conflict with XFCE stuff (gnome-screensaver, gnome-power-manager)

---

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-23
I don't think it's that unusual. I've used XFCE's panel under Gnome and Gnome's panel under XFCE in the past. They're made modular for a reason. Gnome shell has a lot of neat gadgets, but if you're a conventional taskbar person, XFCE's panel might be useful nonetheless.

In any case, it's certainly no more weird than using Gnome Shell with a dock, and plenty of folks do. There are still advantages to the Gnome Shell interface that way.

Personally, I wouldn't - Gnome Shell offers all the UI elements I'd want or need, and all it really seems to be missing for my tastes is an extension for different backdrops per workspace, which is a helpful mimetic tool. But moving from Gnome to XFCE isn't as easy as a lot of folks make it out to be, either. I've tried in the past, personally, and I can't, because XFCE's multiple monitor support is incomprehensible to me.

---

### Post by vehemoth on 2011-10-23
> **stanca said:**
> I edited the .conkyrc file this way: 
```
own_window_type normal
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_argb_visual yes
own_window_argb_value 0
```It works on E17 too.I haven't tried it on KDE4 yet.
Enjoy it! :):P
Yeah I just tried conky out with a compisiting WM for the first time and didn't have the slowness problems I had before, because of this I was able to inside my .conkyrc use a background image that took up the whole window perfectly fine. I'm assuming you did something similar.

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-25
Oh, good, they fixed the exo-utils bug? Under 11.04 (and apparently *only* 11.04,) installing XFCE's panel, Thunar, or some of the others requires exo-utils as you'd expect, but doesn't configure it properly, which breaks xdg-open for locations under Gnome unless you run exo-preferred-applications and fix the associations from there. (Editing mimeapps.list doesn't help.)

---

### Post by ShodanjoDM on 2011-10-25
I guess I've missed the news about exo-utils bugs, but in 11.04, I've installed Thunar (for its batch renamer utility) and didn't experience anything like that.

Infact, 11.04 is still there in another partition although I didn't install any other xfce packages though.

---

### Post by arzali on 2011-10-25
> **Copper Bezel said:**
> Gah, you, too? Stop making me want to switch to Shell. Clutter is crap on my CPU.

Very nice work. Does DockBarX play nicely with Clutter? 

I didn't realize that the shell theme could be applied independent of  the window decorator. That's neat. One possible critique, though, is  that they don't match - the uniform black overlays with lighter trim  mesh, but the Shell elements are rounded and nothing else is. I'd be  tempted to round the corners at least on DockBarX to make it blend a bit  more (but leave the squared window lists you've shown off previously,  like wearing shoes with both black and brown as an excuse to get away  with wearing a black jacket over a brown shirt.)

Thank you and dont worry. I only test gnomeshell, so im still on 10.10
Dockbarx works as nicely as with metacity in older versions (without compiz) and the decorators are bound to the gtk metacity theme, so if you change the gtk theme, the decorators change too (new in 3.2 i think)
About the rounded shell theme, i used elegant brit theme before but then switched to elementary because of the wingpanel :). im still working on it to replace blue with orange and make it square like the brit theme.

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-25
> Thank you and dont worry. I only test gnomeshell, so im still on 10.10
Dockbarx works as nicely as with metacity in older versions (without compiz) and the decorators are bound to the gtk metacity theme, so if you change the gtk theme, the decorators change too (new in 3.2 i think)
About the rounded shell theme, i used elegant brit theme before but then switched to elementary because of the wingpanel :). im still working on it to replace blue with orange and make it square like the brit theme.
Very cool. I'm looking forward to the end result - it's a gorgeous theme. And it makes a lot of sense that Metacity and GTK themes are linked now, for obvious reasons.

In any case, you inspired me to try a Fedora LiveCD (I'm on a puny little SSD that can only really have one OS installed at a time) and while there are a couple of Compiz effects I'd miss, Gnome Shell is wonderful. It's a really grown-up interface and potentially a lot more productive than what I have going now. (I tried the new Unity, and it's nice, too, but not on the same level.) Now if only my trackpad driver worked under the 3.0 kernel. = P

I have to admit, I probably wouldn't use a dock under Shell myself, but it's not because Shell's Favorites list replaces the dock by itself. To me, Favorites is just a rethinking of desktop launchers and doesn't seem as useful for task switching and the like.

---

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-25
goldshirt9 is asking about removing the little Accessibility man from Gnome Shell's *top* bar. It's possible with the [_No A11y extension_]("http://joesteiger.com/2011/07/26/remove-accessibility-menu-with-noa11y-gnome-shell-extension-gnome-3-ubuntu-11-04/"), but it might not work with 3.2.

---

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2011-10-25
> **the little Accessibility man** from Gnome Shell's *top* bar.sorry friend, Still confused. lol O_o

I dunno, Everything in the top bar/panel, I use often.

---

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-25
Look at any of sanderd17's screenshots. To the left of the volume wheel, there's a little man in a circle representing a11y options like zoom and sticky keys. For a single user account, it doesn't make sense to have access to these at all times, so a lot of people remove it. If you don't have it, you probably installed just such an extension without noticing.

---

### Post by Rasa1111 on 2011-10-25

If you don't have it, you probably installed just such an extension without noticing.

### Post by viperdvman on 2011-10-26
New screenshots from my Ubuntu's KDE desktop:

Full-size screenshots here:
[http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuKDE2a.jpg](http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuKDE2a.jpg)
[http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuKDE2b.jpg](http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuKDE2b.jpg)
[http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuKDE2c.jpg](http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuKDE2c.jpg)
[http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuKDEsplash.jpg](http://img.photobucket.com/albums/v245/viperdvman/ScreenshotUbuKDEsplash.jpg)

I like running KDE. It's a great alternative to Unity and GNOME. But best yet, I like the Activities function, and it shows. I have my default desktop, the netbook-style Search & Launch *(you can actually do that in the KDE-Plasma-Desktop)*, and a customized workspace with folder view widgets for my fanfiction.

I have my custom-made Cadillac Ciel background on my main workspace, a wallpaper from KDE-Look on my Search & Launch, and my custom-made Legend of Zelda Link & Saria background on my fanfiction workspace. I'm using the default Air theme and Oxygen icons, a custom menu icon, and Ubuntu colors instead of the Oxygen colors. And last, my splash screen is also from KDE-Look.

I mainly have this desktop environment to play around with KDE Plasma. But, sometimes I'll be in the mood to run KDE instead of GNOME or Unity. Aren't choices with Ubuntu great? :)

How hard would it be to make a entirely new theme for KDE?

I'm thinking something along the lines of Orta, Greybird or OS X. Important things are reducing wasted space. Maybe it's something you can work on so long :biggrin:

### Post by koleoptero on 2011-10-27
> **mips said:**
> How hard would it be to make a entirely new theme for KDE?

I'm thinking something along the lines of Orta, Greybird or OS X. Important things are reducing wasted space. So compact window title bars, thin borders, smaller buttons/widgets (whatever they are called), clean icons (less colours & flash) ala Aw0ken etc. In the end I would like a neat clean sharp interface.

Not that hard. There are plenty of icon themes to choose from. And as for widgets, there's qtcurve and bespin that are very configurable.

### Post by Dondermans on 2011-10-27
> **dpny said:**
> How are you able to run Nord without distortion in the upper left hand corner?

If you mean the distortion shown on the attachment 'UL_corner': one needs to prevent Nautilus from managing the desktop. The setting which needs to be turned off is 'Have file manager handle desktop'  in Gnome Tweaktool (as shown on the attachment 'Tweaktool settings'.

In doing so,  you will lose the desktop icons. If I am not mistaken, that would be the reason to install a screenlet showing the desktop.

---

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-27
Adwaita's nice. It's not that far a cast from Orta, even if it lacks some of the polish - in the notebook tabs and menus, for instance, which are just painfully flat and lifeless. I'd also miss the little curves around the input areas, although those aren't all that common. I love the toolbar and button style, and I like that the decorator theme is smooth with the GTK instead of having a sharp transition or division like Ambiance's.

I can't bring myself to bite the bullet and upgrade, though. From playing with a Fedora LiveCD, Shell seems extraordinarily productive and fun to drive - the Activities overview really is brilliant, particularly with the Zeitgeist extensions added - but it's missing all the little touches. I can't stand that they have such a nice fade / glide transition for opening windows, but don't even play it backward for closing them, so that windows just *vanish*, and I miss the fade transitions I get under Compiz for menus, as well. There are little productivity gaffs, too - I don't understand why the Google and Wikipedia buttons are included in the search if clicking them doesn't even take you to the browser instance they load in. 

Then there's the really nutty stuff like alpha blurring....

So I'm content to stick with this for now. = )

[[img]http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/20111027/copy%20of%20Screenshot-1.png[/img]](http://dl.dropbox.com/u/17749392/Screenshots/20111027/Screenshot-1.png)

---

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2011-10-28
> **Dondermans said:**
> First off, thank you for the suggestion to combine these options together:

GTK3: Adwaita
Window theme: Adwaita
Gnome Shell: Nord
Icon Theme: Faience

My Ubuntu-setup looks better than ever. I also noticed that Imageviewer and Mplayer don't play nice (perhaps there are other applications too). 

Could you give me a few pointers on editing out the dark theme from Adwaita? I have no experience with programming unfortunately. I gathered that it has to do with changing HTML-colours in a .css file, but I would like to know more please.

Sure. It's quick but ugly way and you can't use the dark theme of Adwaita afterwards (unless you reverse these actions).

Simple rename the dark themes in Adwaita.
<alt>+<F2>
```
gksu nautilus
```

go to /usr/share/themes/adwaita/gtk3
change the name of these files, to anything you like (add eg _backup to their names):
gtk-dark.css
gtk-widgets-assets-dark.css
gtk-widgets-dark-overrides.css

---

Oh hey, cool. I'm the same way - I just use my nifty two-finger scroll gesture and wonder what those silly boxes are for the apps that present them - but since I'm on Ubuntu, I get the overlay scrollbars anyway, and they seem to be coming up consistently on the GTK3 apps. (All five of them. = P)

### Post by Perfect Storm on 2011-10-30
It's part of the Ubuntu/unity style. You can uninstall it by:

```
sudo su
echo "export LIBOVERLAY_SCROLLBAR=0" > /etc/X11/Xsession.d/80overlayscrollbars
```

or removing the packages:
```
sudo apt-get remove overlay-scrollbar liboverlay-scrollbar-0.1-0
```

---

### Post by Copper Bezel on 2011-10-30
[QUOTE=Artificial Intelligence]AFAIK, orta GTK2 is using pixbuf GTK2 engine to get it working. I can't see if pixbuf engine is available for GTK3 or if you can use the default engine to make the same stuff.[/QUOTE]
Yeah, that's what I'm trying to figure out - whether or not the complicated tricks pulled by Orta in GTK2 can be worked out in simple ways in GTK3, which is a fairly tall order, but not beyond hope. For instance, the rounded input fields on apps that treat input areas as widgets happen *automatically* in GTK3 if gtk.css has a global setting for rounded edges, and the gradient on menus can be easily defined. Buttons can still be defined as images, etc. So far as I can tell, window gradients can be handled through Unico in a rather straightforward way as well - I just haven't figured it out yet.

You're right that even for GTK2, not all the same tricks work under Gnome 3, so that Orta itself as a GTK2 theme is broken in Gnome 3. Every GTK3 theme needs a GTK2 theme for rendering GTK2 apps, but the engines seem limited in ways they weren't under Gnome 2. I haven't played with this very much, but it does seem that a successful port of Orta would really be two ports, and the results for GTK2 apps might be less than satisfactory.

Unrelated, but I was very sad to see that menus apparently still can't be rounded in GTK3. Yuck.

---
